## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv_dt) depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t. The equation of motion involves nonlinear restoring forces, possible damping, and potential external driving.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (linear with periodic driving)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Van der Pol type: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 + c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (position-dependent stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Driven pendulum: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven damped pendulum)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (combined damping mechanisms)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve oscillator symmetry about equilibrium — use odd polynomial in x
- Nonlinear damping (v*x**2 or v**3 terms) indicates amplitude-dependent energy dissipation — look for velocity-position coupling
- Periodic driving forces appear as sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) when time t is an explicit variable in an oscillator
- Duffing-type hardening/softening behavior manifests as cubic correction: c0*x + c1*x**3 where sign of c1 determines hardening vs softening
- Self-excited oscillations (limit cycles) require velocity terms that change sign with amplitude, e.g., (1 - c*x**2)*v (Van der Pol structure)
- Parametric excitation appears as multiplicative coupling between time-periodic terms and position: x*cos(c*t)
- Conservation of phase-space structure in Hamiltonian systems means no odd powers of v alone (no pure damping) — presence of v terms indicates dissipation
- Pendulum-like large-amplitude behavior replaces linear x with sin(c*x), capturing the bounded nature of angular restoring torque
